# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I have successfully completed the task. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I identified all Java source files implementing Kafka's consumer group partition assignment strategies in the apache/kafka repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489):

### Concrete Assignor Implementations:

1. **RangeAssignor** - Assigns partitions per-topic in numeric order to consumers in lexicographic order
2. **RoundRobinAssignor** - Distributes partitions round-robin across all consumers
3. **StickyAssignor** - Preserves existing assignments while maintaining balance (eager rebalance)
4. **CooperativeStickyAssignor** - Sticky assignment with cooperative rebalancing (fewer revocations)

### Base Classes:

5. **AbstractPartitionAssignor** - Abstract base implementing the ConsumerPartitionAssignor interface with common partition assignment logic
6. **AbstractStickyAssignor** - Extends AbstractPartitionAssignor with shared sticky assignment implementation used by both sticky assignors

All files have been documented in `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the implementation architecture and relationships.

We then divide the number of partitions by the total number of\\n45:  * consumers to determine the number of partitions to assign to each consumer. If it does not evenly\\n46:  * divide, then the first few consumers will have one extra partition.\\n47:  *\\n48:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and\\n49:  * <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>,\\n50:  * <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n51:  *\\n52:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n53:  * <ul>\\n54:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n55:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code></li>\\n56:  * </ul>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\\n59:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n60:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C2</code>.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n63:  * <ul>\\n64:  * <li><code>C3 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1])</code>\\n65:  * <li><code>C2 (was C1): [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n66:  * </ul>\\n67:  *\\n68:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\\n69:  * can be avoided by setting the group.instance.id.\\n70:  * Consumers will have individual instance ids <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>. We attempt to match consumer racks with\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\n89:  * <p>\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\n95:  * </p>\n96:  */\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \"range\";\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\n100: \n101:     @Override\n102:     public String name() {\n103:         return RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME;\n104:     }\n105: \n106:     private Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic(Map<String, Subscription> consumerMetadata) {\n107:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> topicToConsumers = new HashMap<>();\n108:         consumerMetadata.forEach((consumerId, subscription) -> {\n109:             MemberInfo memberInfo = new MemberInfo(consumerId, subscription.groupInstanceId(), subscription.rackId());\n110:             subscription.topics().forEach(topic -> put(topicToConsumers, topic, memberInfo));\n111:         });\n112:         return topicToConsumers;\n113:     }\n114: \n115:     /**\n116:      * Performs range assignment of the specified partitions for the consumers with the provided subscriptions.\n117:      * If rack-awareness is enabled for one or more consumers, we perform rack-aware assignment first to assign\n118:      * the subset of partitions that can be aligned on racks, while retaining the same co-partitioning and\n119:      * per-topic balancing guarantees as non-rack-aware range assignment. The remaining partitions are assigned\n120:      * using standard non-rack-aware range assignment logic, which may result in mis-aligned racks.\n121:      */\n122:     @Override\n123:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignPartitions(Map<String, List<PartitionInfo>> partitionsPerTopic,\n124:                                                               Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\n125:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic = consumersPerTopic(subscriptions);\n126:         Map<String, String> consumerRacks = consumerRacks(subscriptions);\n127:         List<TopicAssignmentState> topicAssignmentStates = partitionsPerTopic.entrySet().stream()\n128:                 .filter(e -> !e.getValue().isEmpty())\n129:                 .map(e -> new TopicAssignmentState(e.getKey(), e.getValue(), consumersPerTopic.get(e.getKey()), consumerRacks))\n130:                 .collect(Collectors.toList());\n131: \n132:         Map<String, topicAssignmentStates.stream().anyMatch(t -> t.needsRackAwareAssignment);\n136:         if (useRackAware)\n137:             assignWithRackMatching(topicAssignmentStates, assignment);\n138: \n139:         topicAssignmentStates.forEach(t -> assignRanges(t, (c, tp) -> true, assignment));\n140: \n141:         if (useRackAware)\n142:             assignment.values().forEach(list -> list.sort(PARTITION_COMPARATOR));\n143:         return assignment;\n144:     }\n145: \n146:     // This method is not used, but retained for compatibility with any custom assignors that extend this class.\n147:     @Override\n148:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assign(Map<String, Integer> partitionsPerTopic,\n149:                                                     Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\n150:         return assignPartitions(partitionInfosWithoutRacks(partitionsPerTopic), subscriptions);\n151:     }\n152: \n153:     private void assignRanges(TopicAssignmentState assignmentState,\n154:                               BiFunction<String, TopicPartition, Boolean> mayAssign,\n155:                               Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n156:         for (String consumer : assignmentState.consumers.keySet()) {\n157:             if (assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.isEmpty())\n158:                 break;\n159:             List<TopicPartition> assignablePartitions = assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.stream()\n160:                     .filter(tp -> mayAssign.apply(consumer, tp))\n161:                     .limit(assignmentState.maxAssignable(consumer))\n162:                     .collect(Collectors.toList());\n163:             if (assignablePartitions.isEmpty())\n164:                 continue;\n165: \n166:             assign(consumer, assignablePartitions, assignmentState, assignment);\n167:         }\n168:     }\n169: \n170:     private void assignWithRackMatching(Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\n171:                                         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n172: \n173:         assignmentStates.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.consumers)).forEach((consumers, states) ->\n174:             states.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.partitionRacks.size())).forEach((numPartitions, coPartitionedStates) -> {\n175:                 if (coPartitionedStates.size() > 1)\n176:                     assignCoPartitionedWithRackMatching(consumers, numPartitions, coPartitionedStates, assignment);\n177:                 else {\n178:                     TopicAssignmentState state =                            int numPartitions,\n188:                                                      Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\n189:                                                      Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n190: \n191:         Set<String> remainingConsumers = new LinkedHashSet<>(consumers.keySet());\n192:         for (int i = 0; i < numPartitions; i++) {\n193:             int p = i;\n194: \n195:             Optional<String> matchingConsumer = remainingConsumers.stream()\n196:                     .filter(c -> It\\n33:  * then proceeds to do a round robin assignment from partition to consumer. If the subscriptions of all consumer\\n34:  * instances are identical, then the partitions will be uniformly distributed. (i.e., the partition ownership counts\\n35:  * will be within a delta of exactly one across all consumers.)\\n36:  *\\n37:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and <code>t1</code>,\\n38:  * and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t0p2</code>,\\n39:  * <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n40:  *\\n41:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n42:  * <ul>\\n43:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p2, t1p1]</code>\\n44:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p0, t1p2]</code>\\n45:  * </ul>\\n46:  *\\n47:  * <p>When subscriptions differ across consumer instances, the assignment process still considers each\\n48:  * consumer instance in round robin fashion but skips over an instance if it is not subscribed to\\n49:  * the topic. We choose to honor\n68:  * the sorted order based on ephemeral <code>member.id</code>.\n69:  *\n70:  * <p>The assignment will be:\n71:  * <ul>\n72:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\n73:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p1]</code>\n74:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\n75:  * </ul>\n76:  *\n77:  * After one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\n78:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C5</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code>, <code>C2</code> -&gt; <code>C4</code>.\n79:  *\n80:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\n81:  * <ul>\n82:  * <li><code>C3 (was C1): [t0p0, t1p0] (before was [t0p1, t1p1])</code>\n83:  * <li><code>C4 (was C2): [t0p1, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\n84:  * <li><code>C5 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t1p0])</code>\n85:  * </ul>\n86:  *\n87:  * This issue could be mitigated by the introduction of static membership. Consumers will have individual instance ids\n88:  * <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>, <code>I3</code>. As long as\n89:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\n90:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\n91:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\n92:  *\n93:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\n94:  * <ul>\n95:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\n96:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p1, t1p1]</code>\n97:  * <li><code>I2: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\n98:  * </ul>\n99:  */\n100: public class RoundRobinAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\n101:     public static final String ROUNDROBIN_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \"roundrobin\";\n102: \n103:     @Override\n104:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assign(Map<String, Integer> partitionsPerTopic,\n105:                                                     Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\n106:         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment = new HashMap<>();\n107:         List<MemberInfo> memberInfoList = new ArrayList<>();\n108:         for (Map.Entry<String, Subscription> memberSubscription : subscriptions.entrySet()) {\n109:             assignment.put(memberSubscription.getKey(), new memberSubscription.getValue().groupInstanceId()));\n112:         }\n113: \n114:         CircularIterator<MemberInfo> assigner = new CircularIterator<>(Utils.sorted(memberInfoList));\n115: \n116: First, it guarantees an assignment that is as balanced as possible, meaning either:\\n38:  * <ul>\\n39:  * <li>the numbers of topic partitions assigned to consumers differ by at most one; or</li>\\n40:  * <li>each consumer that has 2+ fewer topic partitions than some other consumer cannot get any of those topic partitions transferred to it.</li>\\n41:  * </ul>\\n42:  * Second, it preserved as many existing assignment as possible when a reassignment occurs. This helps in saving some of the\n43:  * overhead processing when topic partitions move from one consumer to another.</p>\n44:  *\n45:  * <p>Starting fresh it would work by distributing the partitions over consumers as evenly as possible. Even though this may sound similar to\n46:  * how round robin assignor works, the second example below shows that it is not.\n47:  * During a reassignment it would perform the reassignment in such a way that in the new assignment\n48:  * <ol>\n49:  * <li>topic partitions are still distributed as evenly as possible, and</li>\n50:  * <li>topic partitions stay with their previously assigned consumers as much as possible.</li>\n51:  * </ol>\n52:  * Of course, the first goal above takes precedence over the second one.</p>\n53:  *\n54:  * <p><b>Example 1.</b> Suppose there are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n55:  * four topics <code>t0,</code> <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, <code>t3</code>, and each topic has 2 partitions,\n56:  * resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\n57:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t3p0</code>, <code>t3p1</code>. Each consumer is subscribed to all three topics.\n58:  *\n59:  * The assignment with both sticky and round robin assignors will be:\n60:  * <ul>\n61:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0]</code></li>\n62:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t2p0, t3p1]</code></li>\n63:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p0, t2p1]</code></li>\n64:  * </ul>\n65:  *\n66:  * Now, let's assume <code>C1</code> is removed and a reassignment is about to happen. The round robin assignor would produce:\n67:  * <ul>\n68:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0, t2p0, t3p0]</code></li>\n69:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p1, t1p1, t2p1, t3p1]</code></li>\n70:  * </ul>\n71:  *\n72:  * while the sticky assignor would result in:\n73:  * <ul>\n74:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0, t2p0]</code></li>\n75:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p1, t0p1, t3p1]</code></li>\n76:  * </ul>\n77:  * preserving all the previous assignments (unlike the round robin assignor).\n78:  *</p>\n79:  * <p><b>Example 2.</b> There are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n80:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions respectively.\n81:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\n82:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>. <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>; <code>C1</code> is subscribed to\n83:  * <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>; and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\n84:  *\n85:  * The round robin assignor would come up with the following assignment:\n86:  * <ul>\n87:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\n88:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0]</code></li>\n89:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n90:  * </ul>\n91:  *\n92:  * which is not as balanced as the assignment suggested by sticky assignor:\n93:  * <ul>\n94:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\n95:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\n96:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n97:  * </ul>\n98:  *\n99:  * Now, if consumer <code>C0</code> is removed, these two assignors would produce the following assignments.\n100:  * Round Robin (preserves 3 partition assignments):\n101:  * <ul>\n102:  * <li><code>C1 [t0p0, t1p1]</code></li>\n103:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n104:  * </ul>\n105:  *\n106:  * Sticky (preserves 5 partition assignments):\n107:  * <ul>\n108:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1, t0p0]</code></li>\n109:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n110:  * </ul>\n111:  *</p>\n112:  * <h3>Impact on <code>ConsumerRebalanceListener</code></h3>\n113:  * The sticky assignment strategy can provide some optimization to those consumers that have some partition cleanup code\n114:  * in their <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code> callback listeners. The cleanup code is placed in that callback listener\n115:  * because the consumer has no assumption or hope of preserving any of its assigned partitions after a rebalance when it\n116:  * is using range or round robin assignor. The listener code would look like this:\n117:  * <pre>\n118:  * {@code\n119:  * class TheOldRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n120:  *\n121:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n122:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\n123:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\n124:  *       cleanupState(partition);\n125:  *     }\n126:  *   }\n127:  *\n128:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n129:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\n130:  *       initializeState(partition);\n131:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\n132:  *     }\n133:  *   }\n134:  * }\n135:  * }\n136:  * </pre>\n137:  *\n138:  * As mentioned above, one advantage of the sticky assignor is that, in general, it reduces the number of partitions that\n139:  * actually move from one consumer to another during a reassignment. Therefore, it allows consumers to do their cleanup\n140:  * more efficiently. Of course, they still can perform the partition cleanup in the <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code>\n141:  * listener, but they can be more efficient and make a note of their partitions before and after the rebalance, and do the\n142:  * cleanup after the rebalance only on the partitions they have lost (which is normally not a lot). The code snippet below\n143:  * clarifies this point:\n144:  * <pre>\n145:  * {@code\n146:  * class TheNewRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n147:  *   Collection<TopicPartition> lastAssignment = Collections.emptyList();\n148:  *\n149:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n150:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions)\n151:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\n152:  *   }\n153:  *\n154:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> assignment) {\n155:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(lastAssignment, assignment))\n156:  *       cleanupState(partition);\n157:  *\n158:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(assignment, lastAssignment))\n159:  *       initializeState(partition);\n160:  *\n161:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: assignment)\n162:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\n163:  *\n164:  *     this.lastAssignment = assignment;\n165:  *   }\n166:  * }\n167:  * }\n168:  * </pre>\n169:  *\n170:  * Any consumer that uses sticky assignment can leverage this listener like this:\n171:  * <code>consumer.subscribe(topics, new TheNewRebalanceListener());</code>\n172:  *\n173:  * Note that you can leverage the {@link CooperativeStickyAssignor} so that only partitions which are being\n174:  * reassigned to another consumer will be revoked. That is the preferred assignor for newer cluster. See\n175:  * {@link ConsumerPartitionAssignor.RebalanceProtocol} for a detailed explanation of cooperative rebalancing.\n176:  */\n177: public class StickyAssignor extends AbstractStickyAssignor
